Let me analyze this position carefully. Black has a strong center with pawns on d5 and e5 against White's d4 and b4. White has played the aggressive b4 push, which looks like a kind of gambit setup.

Key considerations:
- I can capture on d4 with ...exd4, opening the center
- I can play ...e4 to gain space
- Developing moves like ...Nf6, ...Bd6, ...Nc6 are natural
- ...Bf8xb4 would win a pawn since the bishop can capture on b4

Wait, ...Bxb4 is available! That captures a pawn and puts pressure on the position. After ...Bxb4, White would need to deal with the bishop on b4, and the c3 pawn is pinned relative to the king if the queen comes to the d-file.

But let me think more carefully. After ...Bxb4, White can play cxb4... no, the pawn is on c3 not c4. After ...Bxb4, White can play Qa4+ or Bd2. After Qa4+, Nc6 blocks nicely and develops. After Bd2, Bxd2+ Qxd2 and Black has won a pawn.

Actually, let me also consider solid development. ...Nf6 is always a good developing move, putting pressure on d4 and developing the kingside. But winning a pawn with ...Bxb4 seems very attractive.

Let me go with the pawn grab - it's concrete and strong.
